{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"24% of People We Polled Think This is the Worst ‘Star Wars’ Movie – and We Actually Agree","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683084","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-389110 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ranking-star-wars-episode-II-700x350.jpg\" alt=\"ranking star wars\" width=\"700\" height=\"350\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ranking-star-wars-episode-II.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ranking-star-wars-episode-II-360x180.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><em>(Welcome to <strong>Survey Says</strong>, a feature where we conduct a movie-related survey for a random group of people and explain why they’re completely right, completely wrong, or somewhere in-between.)</em></p>\n<p>People are pretty passionate about <em><strong>Star Wars. </strong></em>Those movies about events that happened a long time ago in a galaxy far, far away, really get some fans riled up. Naturally, there&#8217;s been a lot of arguments online in the past few years about which <em>Star Wars</em> flick is the worst, in part due to extremely mixed receptions to both <em><strong>The Last Jedi</strong></em> and <em><strong>The Rise of Skywalker</strong></em>. So we figured it might be fun to issue a survey and ask a bunch of people which <em>Star Wars</em> movie was the absolute worst. Everybody and their mother has made some kind of <em>Star Wars </em>ranking, but we&#8217;re here to give you an unofficial group selection.</p>\n<p>The results weren&#8217;t quite what I expected, given the amount of online hatred I&#8217;ve seen directed toward <em>The Last Jedi. </em>Thankfully, it appears that the people surveyed agree with me (<a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/star-wars-movies-ranked/\">and quite a few of the rest of the /Film crew</a>) and rank <em><strong>Attack of the Clones </strong></em>as the worst <em>Star Wars </em>movie.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683084\"></span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683096 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/worststarwar-700x422.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"422\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/worststarwar-700x422.png 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/worststarwar-360x217.png 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/worststarwar-768x463.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>By the Numbers</h2>\n<p>Okay, so this isn&#8217;t the definitive worst <em>Star Wars</em> decision, but it does represent the responses of 611 Americans responding on Survey Monkey! 600-ish people isn&#8217;t a huge survey sample, but maybe it&#8217;s enough data to give us an idea of what the average American movie-goer might think. Maybe. I don&#8217;t know, I&#8217;m just extrapolating here. Probably not. I&#8217;m not a scientist. Go away. Also, it&#8217;s also worth noting that neither <em><strong>Rogue One: A Star Wars Story </strong></em>or <em><strong>Solo: A Star Wars Story</strong></em><em> </em>were included, only the nine-film Skywalker saga. <em><strong>The Empire Strikes Back</strong></em><em> </em>also wasn&#8217;t included, because no one in their right mind would ever call that the worst <em>Star Wars </em>(except maybe Randall from <em><strong>Clerks</strong></em>).</p>\n<p>Without further ado, here are the survey&#8217;s rankings of the worst <em>Star Wars</em> movie according to a bunch of random strangers on the internet:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Attack of the Clones 24.22%</li>\n<li>The Phantom Menace 19.15%</li>\n<li>The Rise of Skywalker 13.75%</li>\n<li>The Last Jedi 11.95%</li>\n<li>A New Hope 11.62%</li>\n<li>Revenge of the Sith 11.13%</li>\n<li>Force Awakens 8.18%</li>\n</ul>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-331214 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-force-awakens-novelization-2-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-force-awakens-novelization-2.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-force-awakens-novelization-2-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-force-awakens-novelization-2-435x186.jpg 435w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Breaking it Down</h2>\n<p><em>Attack of the Clones </em>really runs away with the worst <em>Star Wars </em>movie title here, beating out <em><strong>The Phantom Menace </strong></em>by almost 5%. The second film in the prequel trilogy,<em> Attack of the Clones </em>is a love story with zero chemistry and a political drama with zero intrigue. There are moments here and there that work within the greater <em>Star Wars</em> story, but overall, it&#8217;s just kind of boring. Most of the movie is spent either trying to develop a romance between Amidala (<strong>Natalie Portman</strong>) and Anakin (<strong>Hayden Christensen</strong>) that feels kind of icky since Anakin was just a kid in the previous movie, while Amidala was already an adult. The rest is a bunch of senate meetings, with occasional bursts of action.</p>\n<p><em>The Phantom Menace</em> coming in second is no surprise. It was the first <em>Star Wars </em>movie in a decade and a half, and expectations were high. Instead, many fans were disappointed by the first prequel&#8217;s zany humor and decidedly younger target audience. <em>The Phantom Menace</em> does have that incredible climactic lightsaber battle, which edges it out over the absolute blandness of <em>Attack of the Clones</em>.</p>\n<p>The next two are really no surprise, and often come up in conversation around one another. <strong>J.J. Abrams</strong>&#8216; <em>The Rise of Skywalker</em> and <strong>Rian Johnson</strong>&#8216;s <em>The Last Jedi</em> are both highly contentious among <em>Star Wars </em>fans. Many were frustrated by <em>The Last Jedi</em>&#8216;s decision to turn series hero Luke Skywalker (<strong>Mark Hamill</strong>) into a bitter recluse. They also felt Johnson&#8217;s desire to focus on thematics and meta-context instead of delivery a straightforward <em>Star Wars</em> adventure didn&#8217;t fit in with the series so far, though other fans disagreed. <em>The Rise of Skywalker</em> was a quick about-face on the part of Disney and Lucasfilm, bringing back old fan favorites from the original trilogy and attempting to &#8220;fix&#8221; what fans didn&#8217;t like about <em>The Last Jedi</em>. Both movies have their fans and detractors, and those feelings are pretty intense.</p>\n<p>The biggest surprise here comes from <strong><em>A New Hope</em></strong> being ranked as worse than <em><strong>Revenge of the Sith</strong></em>, which features the goofiest &#8220;No!&#8221; in all of cinema, and <strong><em>The Force Awakens</em></strong>, which is just <em>A New Hope</em> with a fresh coat of paint. It&#8217;s hard to imagine anyone hating on the original <em>Star Wars</em> film, the one that started it all, but clearly some people prefer the updated version. For some reason. What gives, random survey responders?</p>\n<p>Maybe they can&#8217;t rate <em>The Force Awakens</em> as the worst because it&#8217;s relatively forgettable in the grand scheme. It&#8217;s hard to find fault with something you can&#8217;t remember.</p>\n<p>For what it&#8217;s worth, I absolutely agree that <em>Attack of the Clones </em>is the biggest stinker in the <em>Star Wars</em> franchise, but <em>A New Hope</em> ranking at all feels blasphemous. What do you think?</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/worst-star-wars-movie-survey/\">24% of People We Polled Think This is the Worst &#8216;Star Wars&#8217; Movie – and We Actually Agree</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ranking-star-wars-episode-II-700x350.jpg","linkMd5":"fca7b7ecdfbd29b58ef0cc2568048000","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn10@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-07-522_fb1b4788c8f8bc73.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":350,"sourceBytes":47913,"destBytes":21264,"author":"Danielle Ryan","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/ranking-star-wars-episode-II-700x350.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn10@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-07-522_fb1b4788c8f8bc73.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/worststarwar-700x422.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn52@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-14-622_fd337b3cae6a17bf.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-force-awakens-novelization-2-700x300.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn11@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-14-013_3403ffa391d1add4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn76@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-14-413_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=2P64Ehif9LM:T5bAXtSeReE:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn90@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-13-955_7555023f5cdaec6b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn3@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-14-788_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=2P64Ehif9LM:T5bAXtSeReE:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn7@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-14-357_5416087c6ec6ebd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/2P64Ehif9LM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn25@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-13-955_c4343755680c729c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626196915177},{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"‘Pig’ Review: Nicolas Cage Gives One of His Best Performances in This Haunting Drama","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683194","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Pig-Review.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683208\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Pig-Review-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"Pig Review\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Pig-Review-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Pig-Review-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Pig-Review-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Pig-Review.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>&#8220;<strong>Nicolas Cage</strong> is a guy looking for his stolen pig,&#8221; the general premise of <strong>Michael Sarnoski</strong>&#8216;s elegant, haunting, mournful movie <strong><em>Pig</em></strong>, likely inspires more than a few assumptions. You&#8217;d be forgiven for assuming that a movie like that would be some sort of goofy, indie <em>John Wick </em>knock-off. You&#8217;d also be forgiven for assuming that Cage, playing the man searching for his pilfered porcine pal, goes over the top. After all, Cage has become legendary for becoming unhinged on screen. And he&#8217;s become notorious for appearing in a lot of junk, too.</p>\n<p>But within moments of starting, <em>Pig</em> demands you leave all those assumptions behind you. Because <em>Pig</em> is not the movie you think it is. It&#8217;s something far more beautiful, and far more painful. It is an existential meditation on the search for <em>something. Anything</em>. A kind of cosmic loneliness envelopes this film. It&#8217;s extraordinary.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683194\"></span></p>\n<p>Cage is Rob, a mysterious, grizzled man who lives out in the wilderness with only his truffle-hunting pig for company. By day, Rob and the pig take to the woods in search of fancy fungi. By night, they return to a ramshackle cabin, where the pig has its own little bed mere inches away from Rob&#8217;s. The only real human contact Rob has is with Amir (<strong>Alex Wolff</strong>), a hotshot trying to make a name for himself in the Portland restaurant scene. Amir stops by in his cool car on Thusdays to purchase Rob&#8217;s truffles.</p>\n<p>Rob&#8217;s life is simple, quiet. Watching him is like watching part of the scenery – as if the character is blending into the nature he inhabits. These early moments have an earthy quality that teases our scenes; we can smell the woods, the dirt, the small little private world Rob inhabits. But this tranquility will not last. Late one night, a pair of drug addicts burst into Rob&#8217;s home, knock him out, and steal his pig. It&#8217;s a harrowing, horrifying scene, made all the more disturbing by the human-like screams emitting from the kidnapped pig. It breaks your heart.</p>\n<p>Here is where you might think the movie turns into <em>John Wick But With a Pig Instead of a Dog</em>. &#8220;Ah-ha!&#8221; you might say after the big, brutal pig snatching scene. &#8220;Now Nic Cage is going to go <em>crazy</em> and enact bloody revenge against those who wronged him!&#8221; But remember: <em>Pig</em> is not the movie you think it is. Bloody and bruised, Rob picks himself up and sets out to find his pig, dragging Amir along with him. Rob has no means of transportation, so Amir becomes his reluctant chauffeur.</p>\n<p>As Rob and Amir search for the pig, Rob&#8217;s backstory comes clearer into focus. We learn he was once a renowned chef, but that he&#8217;s been off the grid for 15 years. That time away hasn&#8217;t diminished his celebrity, though. If anything, it&#8217;s made it stronger. When Rob enters a restaurant and the people working there realize who he is, they&#8217;re awed, as if they&#8217;re having some sort of religious experience. As if Rob was the Pope and they were the faithful ready to bury their faces in his vestments.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pig-movie.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683209\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pig-movie-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pig-movie-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pig-movie-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pig-movie-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pig-movie.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Writer-director Sarnoski does a fair amount of subtle world-building here. Rob and Amir are not moving through the restaurant scene as you or I would. They&#8217;re instead traveling through backrooms and places where regular customers would not be welcome. A surreal quality unfolds here, as if we&#8217;re not entirely sure if what we&#8217;re witnessing is meant to be taken seriously, or if it&#8217;s supposed to be some heightened, fantasized underground world. It&#8217;s a world where things can get violent, and nasty. Where secret chef fight clubs take place in basements and dank rooms that have never experienced a single sliver of sunlight.</p>\n<p>Rob moves through this world seeming both at ease and an outsider. He knows he&#8217;s a legend; he knows he is a chef unlike any other. But he also wants to be left alone. Were it not for his pig, he would not be bothering with this world again. Cage plays all of this with a subtle grace that is bound to shock folks who have come to (wrongly) believe that the actor plays everything big and loud. Yes, Cage can go coo-coo sometimes – there&#8217;s no arguing against that. Yet there is so much more to the actor&#8217;s talents that so many people willingly overlook. They want Cage to be a walking meme, and Cage seems willing to indulge this – up to a point. But he&#8217;s also capable of true nuance, and beauty. He&#8217;s one of our most fascinating working actors, and here he delivers one of the best performances of his entire career. A soulful, introspective, melancholy performance that is so strong, so present, that it carries real weight.</p>\n<p>Wolff makes for a great companion on this journey. His twitchy, blustery character is constantly acting bigger than he really is, and just as we learn more about Rob as the story unfolds, we also learn more about Amir, and his background involving a demanding, powerful father, played by <strong>Adam Arkin</strong>, who shows up late in the film and makes quite an impression, making sure every single second of his small screentime counts.</p>\n<p>Rob is a lost soul, and as we all are in our own little ways. He&#8217;s not just searching for his pig, he&#8217;s also searching for some sort of truth, some sort of beauty. His cooking is his art, and it&#8217;s something perhaps too pure to share with the world regularly. Perhaps that&#8217;s why he dropped off the face of the earth and hid his gifts away. Now, as he continues his search, he once again finds himself cooking for others. They bite into Rob&#8217;s food and unlock memories and dreams long since tucked away and lost. <em>Pig</em> is a lot like Rob&#8217;s food, awakening something within us. We come away changed, tears in our eyes. <em>Pig</em> is not the movie you think it is.</p>\n<p><strong>/Film Rating: 9 out of 10</strong></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/pig-review/\">&#8216;Pig&#8217; Review: Nicolas Cage Gives One of His Best Performances in This Haunting Drama</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=3DtkZRQxHVE:c-Puhb62FtI:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img Evangelista","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Pig-Review-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn28@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-21-55-346_b799415f07d45439.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pig-movie-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn39@2020_3/2021/07/13/17-22-14-540_9c6987b0ed67cc2c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn76@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-14-413_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=3DtkZRQxHVE:c-Puhb62FtI:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn80@2020_3/2021/07/13/17-22-14-506_b257eef41c6e799d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn3@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-14-788_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=3DtkZRQxHVE:c-Puhb62FtI:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn47@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-14-142_429761d4264ab873.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/3DtkZRQxHVE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn56@2020_3/2021/07/13/17-22-13-957_982bde3323badcdd.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626196915177},{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"‘Spriggan’ Trailer: Netflix’s Sci-Fi Action Anime Gets Delayed to 2022","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683192","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683214 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Spriggan-Teaser-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Spriggan-Teaser-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Spriggan-Teaser-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Spriggan-Teaser-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Netflix</strong> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/netflix-anime-deals/\">continues to expand</a> its slate of original anime films and TV shows, but viewers will have to wait a little while longer before they see <em><strong>Spriggan</strong></em>. The series, based on the best-selling manga by <strong>Hiroshi Takashige</strong> and <strong>Ryoji Minagawa</strong>, has been bumped to 2022. In the meantime, the streamer has released a new official teaser to whet your appetite.</p>\n<p>As a manga, <em>Spriggan </em>has sold over ten million copies worldwide. It was originally serialized from 1989 to 1996 in Shogakukan&#8217;s <em>Weekly Shonen Sunday </em>magazine (which, for some reason, publishes on Wednesday, not Sunday). Anime was beginning to find more of a Western audience with movies like <em>Akira</em> and <em>Ghost in the Shell, </em>and <em>Spriggan</em> soon capitalized on this with its own film adaptation, which hit theaters in Japan in 1998 and eventually made its way stateside in 2001.</p>\n<p>Now, a new TV anime adaptation is headed to Netflix. The first teaser for <em>Spriggan</em>, which debuted back in October 2020, ended with the words &#8220;coming 2021.&#8221; This new teaser changes that to &#8220;coming 2022.&#8221;</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683192\"></span></p>\n<h2>Spriggan Official Teaser Trailers</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/PJnbniBJrvQ?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Bombastic music, crackling energy, agents in armored muscle suits, and the secrets of ancient civilizations are all on display in these trailers. <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spriggan\">&#8220;Spriggan&#8221;</a> is actually a word derived from a creature in Cornish folklore. The official synopsis for <em>Spriggan</em> describes the Netflix series in these terms:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p dir=\"auto\">This story depicts the adventures of Yu Ominae, a young man who serves as a “Spriggan,” a special agent of the ARCAM corporation, an organization established to seal away the relics of an ancient civilization.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p dir=\"auto\">In case you missed it, the first teaser reveals more details of the mythological backstory behind <em>Spriggan</em>:</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/XyM77kuOCxQ?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The official logline also goes into greater depth about what Netflix subscribers can expect to see next year:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p dir=\"auto\">A great civilization once existed on this Earth. Possessing knowledge and scientific prowess far exceeding that of modern man, the relics of this ancient civilization remain hidden across this world even now. As high-speed communications networks cover the globe and the peering eyes of satellites are able to expose all secrets, the armies of great nations clash as they seek to uncover and research these artifacts, which possess an unfathomable “power.” A member of this ancient civilization carved a message into a plate: “Protect our legacy from evildoers.” Taking this message to heart, one organization aims to seal away this ancient civilization for good. The elite secret agents of this organization are known as&#8230; Spriggans.</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><em>Spriggan</em> is directed by <strong>Hiroshi Kobayashi</strong> and adapted for the screen by writer <strong>Hiroshi Seko</strong>. <strong>Shuhei Handa</strong> acts as the supervising animation director and is handling the character design. The series features the voices of <strong>Chiaki Kobayashi</strong>, <strong>Youhei Azakami</strong>, <strong>Kenji Hamada</strong>, and <strong>Mariya Ise</strong>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Expect to see <em>Spriggan</em> hit Netflix sometime in <strong>2022</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/spriggan-trailer-release-date/\">&#8216;Spriggan&#8217; Trailer: Netflix&#8217;s Sci-Fi Action Anime Gets Delayed to 2022</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Then you came to the right place! (If you&#8217;re in the wrong place please locate a directory at the nearest kiosk.) In a new featurette, director<strong> James Gunn</strong> talks about the RED cameras he used to shoot the film – including &#8220;a dynamic shooting style that&#8230;wasn’t possible before the creation of RED’s latest camera innovations.&#8221; And while all of this RED talk kind of makes this video feel like an ad, you&#8217;re still getting some new <em>Suicide Squad</em> footage, so that has to count for something.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683297\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>The Suicide Squad Featurette </strong></h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/oss4zPd8bIk?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p><em>The Suicide Squad</em> was filmed entirely with IMAX-certified RED cameras – a process that James Gunn speaks highly of. &#8220;The way that movie is shot is the way I’ve wanted to shoot every movie but have not been able to until now,&#8221; Gunn says in the video above. &#8220;Nearly every shot in this movie is on the move,” says Gunn, “and not only that but we wanted to get up close and move around and between people. The tech has advanced to match what I see with my mind.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Cinematographer<strong> Henry Braham</strong> and his team &#8220;made customized gyrostabilized mounts to enable genuinely stabilized hand-held movement.&#8221; Cameras used included the Ranger Monstro and the Komodo, which was still in prototype at the time. &#8220;Komodo is a great little camera,&#8221; Braham says. &#8220;There are shots in the movie we could only get with something that small that comes with high-res imagery.&#8221; Braham used Leica M-System glass to keep &#8220;image quality and maneuverability in mind.&#8221; “</p>\n<p>&#8220;From the beginning, one of the main goals was to keep it alive, keep it visceral, keep it real; one of the pathways to do that is the way to use the camera,&#8221; Gunn says, adding: &#8220;Nearly every shot in this movie is moving&#8230;and not only is it moving, but we want to get in really close, and between people, and you just can&#8217;t do that with a bulky camera.&#8221; Gunn also says that thanks to the cameras, not only is he getting exactly what he envisioned, he&#8217;s getting <em>better</em> than what he envisioned, adding that the end result was the most enjoyable process he&#8217;s ever had making a film.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Suicide-Squad-Polka-Dot-Man.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-680331\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Suicide-Squad-Polka-Dot-Man-700x300.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Suicide-Squad-Polka-Dot-Man.png 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Suicide-Squad-Polka-Dot-Man-360x154.png 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>The Suicide Squad</strong></h2>\n<p>In <em>The Suicide Squad</em>, Amanda Waller assembles &#8220;a collection of cons, including Bloodsport, Peacemaker, Captain Boomerang, Ratcatcher 2, Savant, King Shark, Blackguard, Javelin and everyone’s favorite psycho, Harley Quinn. Then arm them heavily and drop them (literally) on the remote, enemy-infused island of Corto Maltese. Trekking through a jungle teeming with militant adversaries and guerrilla forces at every turn, the Squad is on a search-and-destroy mission with only Colonel Rick Flag on the ground to make them behave…and Amanda Waller’s government techies in their ears, tracking their every movement. And as always, one wrong move and they’re dead (whether at the hands of their opponents, a teammate, or Waller herself). If anyone’s laying down bets, the smart money is against them—all of them.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Look for <em>The Suicide Squad</em> in theaters and on HBO Max on <strong>August 6, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"The Daily Stream: ‘Summer Wars’ Signaled the Arrival of a New Anime Auteur, But Mamoru Hosoda is More Than “The Next Miyazaki”","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683230","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683244\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/summer-wars-e1626182150948-700x299.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/summer-wars-e1626182150948-700x300.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/summer-wars-e1626182150948-360x154.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/summer-wars-e1626182150948-768x328.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/summer-wars-e1626182150948.jpeg 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><i data-stringify-type=\"italic\">(Welcome to </i><b data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><i data-stringify-type=\"italic\">T</i></b><b data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><i data-stringify-type=\"italic\">he Daily Stream</i></b><i data-stringify-type=\"italic\">, an ongoing series in which the /Film team shares what they’ve been watching, why it’s worth checking out, and where you can stream it.)</i></p>\n<p><strong>The Movie:</strong> <em>Summer Wars</em></p>\n<p><strong>Where You Can Stream It:</strong> Funimation</p>\n<p><strong>The Pitch:</strong> Timid high school junior and math genius Kenji Koiso is strong-armed into posing as the boyfriend for fellow student Natsuki Shinohara, a spirited high school senior who drags Kenji to the rural town of Ueda for her great-grandmother&#8217;s 90th birthday. But after Keji receives a cryptic code on his cell phone and cracks it, he becomes the primary suspect for hacking of OZ, a vibrant virtual world that features everything from fun interactive minigames to the world&#8217;s traffic infrastructure. It&#8217;s up to Kenji to repair the damage and stop the rogue computer program responsible for the hacking.</p>\n<p><strong>Why It’s Essential Viewing:</strong> Mamoru Hosoda&#8217;s <em>Belle</em> is set to make its world premiere at Cannes this week, and with the sci-fi romantic adventure looking to <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/belle-trailer-mamoru-hosoda/\">retread some old ground</a> for the director, <em>Summer Wars</em> and its slice-of-life story meets digital extravaganza is a must-watch.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683230\"></span></p>\n<p>In 2006, Mamoru Hosoda made his big breakthrough with <em>The Girl Who Leapt Through Time</em>, a lovely sci-fi romance that remains <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/hoai-tran-buis-favorite-movies-of-all-time/\">one of my favorite movies</a> of all time. But promising new anime filmmakers are a dime a dozen, and it takes more than one masterpiece to have one name&#8217;s bandied around as the &#8220;next Hayao Miyazaki.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Enter <em>Summer Wars</em>, Hosoda&#8217;s impossibly imaginative digital adventure, which takes all of the filmmaker&#8217;s sleek sci-fi chops that he honed during his time as an animator on <em>Digimon</em> (later making his feature directorial debut with <em>Digimon: The Movie</em>) and combines them with the delicate slice-of-life sensibilities that he had tested out with <em>The Girl Who Leapt Through Time</em>. It&#8217;s hard to describe <em>Summer Wars</em> without it sounding like the weirdest and most <em>anime</em> movie out there, but Hosoda strikes an incredible balance between the wildly differing tones — and genres — of the movie. At first, <em>Summer Wars</em> unfolds like a serene, lazy slice-of-life movie, set in a countryside house where nothing happens outside of a crowded family reunion, where all kinds of outrageous characters vie for the attention of our quiet protagonist. But suddenly, Hosoda shifts gears, and <em>Summer Wars</em> transforms into an action-packed adventure that threatens to overwhelm your senses. It&#8217;s like watching a beaten-up vintage buggy morph into a giant multi-colored mech — and it&#8217;s awesome.</p>\n<p>The virtual-reality scenes are some of the most breathtaking depictions of the digital world that have been rendered to the screen — in both the animated and live-action realm. It&#8217;s exciting, and colorful, and amorphous, with users taking on all kinds of non-human avatars that look like your <em>Alice in Wonderland </em>dreams come to life. And as overwhelming as the imagery can be, it&#8217;s 10 times more watchable than the gray, washed-out depictions of the digital world that Hollywood seems so fond of. Couple that with the warm, pastel tones of the real world, and <em>Summer Wars</em> is a veritable visual feast.</p>\n<p>But let me walk back the &#8220;next Hayao Miyazaki&#8221; label, because I find it to be a reductive way to try to assess anime filmmakers, who can offer so much more than aping the anime titan. Hosoda himself had bucked the Ghibli influence, having been attached at one point to direct the studio&#8217;s <em>Howl&#8217;s Moving Castle</em> before exiting the project over creative differences. Hosoda may operate in some of the same territory as Miyazaki — the pastoral imagery of <em>Summer Wars</em> and the spirit-world locales of his later films like <em>The Boy and the Beast</em> would draw the most comparisons — but he is a very different filmmaker. (And even more different than the other anime auteur who also gets frequently compared to Miyazaki, <em>Your Name</em>&#8216;s <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/weathering-with-you-review/\">Makoto Shinkai</a>.)</p>\n<p>There is an&#8230;ordinariness to Hosoda&#8217;s works, an earthy warmth that surpasses even that of the cosmically-minded Shinkai and the idyllic Miyazaki. Despite the fantastical nature of many of Hosoda&#8217;s films, they feel lived-in, in a way that other anime films can&#8217;t achieve. There&#8217;s a complexity, a messiness to his characters and worlds that make Hosoda more than just the &#8220;next Miyazaki.&#8221; And you can see the beginnings of that in <em>Summer Wars</em>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-daily-stream-summer-wars/\">The Daily Stream: &#8216;Summer Wars&#8217; Signaled the Arrival of a New Anime Auteur, But Mamoru Hosoda is More Than &#8220;The Next Miyazaki&#8221;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"Richard E. Grant Has a Pitch for His Own ‘Loki’ Spin-Off and It Involves Alligator Loki","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683263","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-681285 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/arc-105-11768_r_26412c77-e1625667571651-700x339.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"339\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/arc-105-11768_r_26412c77-e1625667571651.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/arc-105-11768_r_26412c77-e1625667571651-360x174.jpeg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Is there any actor in the business right now who&#8217;s having more fun than <strong>Richard E. Grant</strong>? In recent years, the esteemed thespian has shown up in <em>Game of Thrones</em> as a hilariously snobbish actor in a traveling play, as &#8220;Shiver&#8221; in Disney&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/nutcracker-and-the-four-realms-review/\">bizarrely compelling <em>The Nutcracker and the Four Realms</em></a> (a movie and a performance than I&#8217;m 50% sure I must have hallucinated), and lived out his dream as a First Order officer in <em>The Rise of Skywalker</em>. It was an utter coup for Marvel to grab him for their ongoing <em><strong>Loki</strong></em> series and Grant has some tongue-in-cheek ideas about where to take things next.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683263\"></span></p>\n<h2>Let Richard E. Grant Do Whatever He Wants</h2>\n<p>Not content to stop at merely putting on those Loki horns in that absurdly perfect outfit, the &#8220;Classic Loki&#8221; actor outlines his very serious conditions for coming back to play the character in some future project, especially since (spoiler alert) nobody ever really stays dead in these things anyway. In an interview with <a href=\"https://ew.com/tv/richard-e-grant-loki-interview/\">Entertainment Weekly</a>, Grant offered a pitch for a Classic Loki series:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;If I had a muscle suit, most certainly. I was denied that. I saw the costume design, and I was very familiar with Jack Kirby&#8217;s original illustrations from the &#8217;60s, so I thought, &#8216;Ah, this guy&#8217;s got muscles!&#8217; As I had been born without any, I was finally going to get in a muscle suit. I got to Atlanta [to begin filming], and they said, &#8216;There&#8217;s no muscle suit! You&#8217;re just wearing this!&#8217; I said, &#8216;<a href=\"https://twitter.com/RichardEGrant/status/1412887615204888586\">But I look like Kermit the Frog!</a>&#8216; They said, &#8216;Nope, you&#8217;re not having a muscle suit.&#8217; So I was very, very upset about that. [Laughs] Short-changed!&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-681484\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Alligator-Loki-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Alligator Loki\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Alligator-Loki.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Alligator-Loki-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>See You Later Alligator</h2>\n<p>So what would a Classic Loki series look like, muscle suit aside? According to Grant, it would involve that <a href=\"https://twitter.com/iamkateherron/status/1412675558484451329\">infamously demanding costar</a>, Alligator Loki:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;Alligator Loki was fantastic because in reality, he was three stuffed sofa cushions that had been sewn roughly together to react to. [Laughs] The fact that I was the only person that could understand what he was saying was just fantastic. I think it&#8217;s the perfect segue into having Classic Old Loki and Alligator Loki as a sub-series to go to next.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;I am the Doctor Dolittle of the Marvel universe when it comes to speaking to alligators. I speak alligator fluently. Put that in the contract of when I&#8217;m doing a series as Classic Old Loki, with muscles and the alligator. It&#8217;ll have subtitles, so the audience can hear what the alligator is saying, and everyone else is saying, &#8216;What is he saying? What is he talking about?&#8217; That&#8217;ll be the way.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>There probably aren&#8217;t many MCU projects at this point that crowds <em>wouldn&#8217;t</em> turn out in droves to see, but I feel reasonably confident that <em>The Further Adventures of Classic Loki and Alligator Loki</em> would be a smash hit on Disney+, or even as a movie of its own. Hit me up, Marvel. Grant and I will be patiently awaiting your calls.</p>\n<p>Be sure to <a href=\"https://ew.com/tv/richard-e-grant-loki-interview/\">click through for more tidbits</a> from the interview, ranging from Grant&#8217;s torrid romance with costar <strong>Owen Wilson</strong> to the practicality of shooting those CGI-heavy scenes.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/richard-e-grant-classic-loki-spin-off/\">Richard E. Pains","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683241","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683248\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/turning-red-e1626183239528-700x299.jpg\" alt=\"turning red trailer\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Any studio on the level of <strong>Pixar</strong> is going to be placed under its fair share of scrutiny, as it certainly seems like recent years have led to even more close attention paid to each and every one of their films. Have they finally lost their spark? Is the Golden Age over and done with? Well, <em>Luca</em> was certainly a <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/luca-review/\">slight-but-sweet little tale</a> and now Pixar&#8217;s latest, <em><strong>Turning Red</strong></em>, is angling to have its own say on the matter as well. Pixar released the first teaser trailer earlier today, which you can check out below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683241\"></span></p>\n<h2>Turning Red Teaser Trailer</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/pqdHP2dWQ9M?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Written and directed by <strong>Domee Shi</strong>, best known for her stunning 2018 Oscar-winning short film <em><strong>Bao</strong></em> (which she wrote, directed, and is also credited as story artist) as well as serving in the animation department for <em><strong>Inside Out</strong></em>, <em><strong>The Good Dinosaur</strong></em>, <em><strong>Incredibles 2</strong></em>, and <em><strong>Toy Story 4</strong></em>, <em>Turning Red</em> has the feel of serving as a well-earned promotion for the Pixar veteran.</p>\n<p>The story follows a young teenage girl named Mei Lee (<strong>Rosalie Chiang</strong>) who, in classic Pixar style, transforms into a giant red panda at the slightest hint of excitement. Of course, conflict arises as her overprotective mother Ming (<strong>Sandra Oh</strong>) is constantly hovering over Mei&#8217;s shoulder. As spelled out in the teaser, this premise appears to be a really clever and fun metaphor for the growing pains involved in teenagers struggling to get out from under their stifling parents.</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-588291\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pixaranimation-frontgates-700x312.jpg\" alt=\"A Day in the Life at Pixar Animation\" width=\"700\" height=\"312\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pixaranimation-frontgates-700x312.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pixaranimation-frontgates-360x161.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pixaranimation-frontgates-768x342.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/pixaranimation-frontgates.jpg 888w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>If It Ain&#8217;t Broke&#8230;</h2>\n<p>Like <em>Luca</em> earlier this year or especially something like <em><strong>Coco</strong></em>, outsized (and sometimes very literal) metaphors for such universal, yet culturally-specific concepts tend to be familiar areas that Pixar has excelled at in the past. <em>Turning Red</em> clearly has no shortage of talent supporting this endearingly awkward story and looks set to continue that exciting trend. Based entirely on <em>Bao</em> and its strong ties to Chinese culture, I would certainly not bet against whatever Shi has up her sleeves on this one.</p>\n<p>Honestly, you can count me among the group of dissenters who&#8217;ve been slightly worried that Pixar has somewhat lost its touch in recent years, pivoting to uninspired sequels or prequels and even lacking that special &#8220;something&#8221; in their recent originals, too. Funny how a glimpse of some fun footage can go a long way.</p>\n<p><em>Turning Red</em> is set to bow on <strong>March 11, 2022</strong>. Check out the official synopsis below.</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;Young actress Rosalie Chiang lends her voice to Mei Lee, a 13-year-old who suddenly ‘poofs’ into a giant red panda when she gets too excited (which is practically ALWAYS). Sandra Oh voices Mei Lee’s protective, if not slightly overbearing mother, Ming, who is never far from her daughter—an unfortunate reality for the teenager.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>The post <a 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"The Slashfilmcast is Now The Filmcast – Here’s What You Need to Know","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682246","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/thefilmcasthorizontal.jpg\"><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682257 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/thefilmcasthorizontal-700x299.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/thefilmcasthorizontal-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/thefilmcasthorizontal-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/thefilmcasthorizontal-768x329.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>14 years ago, /Film editor-in-chief Peter Sciretta called me and made me an offer: &#8220;How would you like to make a film podcast for slashfilm.com?&#8221;</p>\n<p>After thinking about it for six minutes, my co-hosts and I decided to do it. How could we refuse? For me, it was a dream come true. I&#8217;d read sites like /Film since I was in high school and I&#8217;d been making podcasts since people listened to them using iPods with clickwheels on them. To be able to make a podcast about movies that more than 30 people might listen to? Of course I had to take the plunge.</p>\n<p><strong>The Slashfilmcast</strong> has been running for over 13 years now. Being able to create this podcast consistently with Devindra and Jeff (and previously, Adam) has been one of the most enjoyable and rewarding experiences of my life. It&#8217;s outlasted several jobs, moves across the country, and host changes. There are undoubtedly be more changes to come in the future, but one of them happens today: <strong>The Slashfilmcast is spinning off to become our own independent podcast called &#8220;The Filmcast.&#8221;</strong> A few reflections and details follow.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682246\"></span></p>\n<p>The Slashfilmcast spawned because I wanted to have a conversation with folks about movies that didn&#8217;t end after someone said, &#8220;That was pretty good!&#8221; I loved diving into spoilers with my colleagues and reflecting on the meaning of movies, along with their cultural significance. We also were grateful and honored by all the guests that stopped by to add their voices to the conversation.</p>\n<p>Our first episode received around a thousand downloads. In the time since then, a lot has happened. We&#8217;ve had guests such as Rian Johnson, James Cameron, and Richard Kelly. The podcast has gone on to be downloaded over 50 million times. A community has formed around the show. Listeners have met and even gotten married because they met through the podcast. New podcasts have spawned from the Slashfilmcast. Hosts have met and formed new ventures because of work we&#8217;ve all done together.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s hard to understate how much all this has meant to me personally. As a kid who grew up in a tiny suburb of Boston, watching Hong Kong action movies and dreaming about Hollywood, I got to actually talk with people who make movies (and occasionally, people would actually listen to our conversations)! I got to learn so much more about how movies were made and distributed, and eventually even <a href=\"http://www.theprimaryinstinct.com\">make a movie myself</a>. Perhaps most importantly, I got to meet and become friends with so many wonderful, talented individuals. Many of these connections will last for the rest of my life.</p>\n<p>Since we launched the show, the world of podcasting has exploded. The tools became easier to use and podcasting no longer required an Intel Core 2 Duo desktop computer with a Sound Blaster. Now, anyone with a smartphone can now make and distribute their own podcast. On the other end, well-financed companies are pouring millions of dollars into creating and distributing podcasts about every single conceivable topic, including movies.</p>\n<p>Simultaneously, the movie industry is in a challenging place right now, especially with theaters shutting down in light of all the events of the past year. I obviously can&#8217;t do those events justice in this post, but suffice it to say that with all the other immense tragedy and upheaval that society as a whole was dealing with, I was honestly unsure whether the show would be able to continue.</p>\n<p>But when <a href=\"http://www.patreon.com/filmpodcast\">we launched our Patreon page</a> last fall, our listeners declared clearly and decisively: They want the show to go on. And so, we will continue. We are extremely grateful for their support, and spinning off independently ensures we can do that in the strongest possible way and under circumstances where we can own our own future.</p>\n<p>Alright, here are some FAQs.</p>\n<h2><strong>Whoa, you&#8217;re not the Slashfilmcast anymore? Did you guys have a fight with /Film or something?</strong></h2>\n<p>Not at all! We love all the fine folks at /Film and you should still expect them to appear occasionally in future episodes of the podcast. We&#8217;ve just been talking about why it might make sense to spin off for awhile now and <a href=\"http://patreon.com/filmpodcast\">our recent support from Patrons</a> has shown us that an independent future is viable. So, we&#8217;re making the leap!</p>\n<h2><strong>What else is going to change about the podcast?</strong></h2>\n<p>Other than the name, we don&#8217;t plan to change anything! We&#8217;ll continue to make the same stuff we&#8217;ve always been making with interesting guests from around the internet and the world of film and television. The podcast will continue to come out weekly (with an After Dark several times per month for patrons). That said, you&#8217;ll no longer see updates/content from the podcast on slashfilm.com.</p>\n<h2><strong>What if I&#8217;m already subscribed to the podcast? Do I need to re-subscribe somewhere else?</strong></h2>\n<p>No. If you&#8217;re already subscribed, you&#8217;ll still get episodes in the existing feed like normal. Just note that our name and podcast icon may look a little different in your podcast app.</p>\n<h2><strong>What if I&#8217;m an existing Patron? Will anything change?</strong></h2>\n<p>No, other than the name of the podcast and podcast icon. <a href=\"http://patreon.com/filmpodcast\">Our tiers</a> will stay the same and you&#8217;ll continue to get ad-free/bonus episodes through the existing feeds.</p>\n<h2><strong>Where can I find older episodes of the podcast?</strong></h2>\n<p>The current podcast feed contains the 250-plus most recent episodes of the podcast. There are no immediate plans to make episodes older than that widely available.</p>\n<h2><strong>Cool new logo! Will you guys have any merch?</strong></h2>\n<p>Stay tuned!</p>\n<h2><strong>Yes, but HOW do I stay tuned? Can I follow you guys on Twitter?</strong></h2>\n<p>Yes, find us at <a href=\"http://twitter.com/thefilmcastpod\">@thefilmcastpod</a>. You&#8217;ll also find our new podcast page at <a href=\"http://thefilmcast.com\">thefilmcast.com</a>. Our email address slashfilmcast(AT)gmail(DOT)com will also continue to function for a little while longer, so you are welcome to reach us there.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center;\">***</p>\n<p>In closing, I want to thank all the fine folks at /Film for their support through this process. And I want to thank Peter Sciretta, for giving a kid a chance in the world of online podcasting. It changed everything.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-slashfilmcast-is-now-the-filmcast-heres-what-you-need-to-know/\">The Slashfilmcast is Now The Filmcast sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s that time again&#8230; time to celebrate the best of television entertainment! The <strong>73rd Primetime Emmy Awards</strong> will give us a chance to cheer for all of the small-screen champions who kept us somewhat sane during the past year. The golden era of television is only getting more glorious, with streaming services competing to deliver the absolute best entertainment possible. It means there&#8217;s a lot to choose from and sift through, but more content means, in this case, more good content.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683277\"></span></p>\n<p>The Outstanding Drama Series category is a real trip this year, with heady historical dramas (<em><strong>The Crown</strong></em>, <em><strong>Bridgerton</strong></em>) facing down a superhero farce (<strong><em>The Boys</em></strong>) and the latest in the <em>Star Wars </em>universe (<em><strong>The Mandalorian</strong></em>). Disney&#8217;s <strong><em>WandaVision</em></strong> and <em><strong>Hamilton</strong></em> are both set to sweep the Limited Series and movie categories, with nine nominations between them. <em><strong>Ted Lasso</strong></em> is the comedy contender for the night with eight nominations, but it&#8217;s the drama <em><strong>The Handmaid</strong></em><strong><em>&#8216;s Tale</em></strong> that earned the most nods, scoring a whopping 11 nominations!</p>\n<p>&#8220;Virtual events kept us connected when we all needed it most, but I&#8217;m ready to celebrate face to face,&#8221; Television Academy Chairman and CEO Frank Scherma said in the live nominations announcement. The 73rd Primetime Emmy Awards will be an in-person event for all of its nominees to attend, a stark contrast from last year&#8217;s virtual show. It should feel like a return to a bit of normalcy, where we can celebrate <em>The Handmaid&#8217;s Tale</em> instead of feeling like we&#8217;re living through it.</p>\n<p>Check out the list of the biggest 2021 Emmy nominations below.</p>\n<h2>2021 Emmy Nominations</h2>\n<p><strong>Outstanding Drama Series:</strong></p>\n<p><em>The Boys<br />\n</em><em>Bridgerton<br />\n</em><em>The Crown<br />\n</em><em>The Handmaid&#8217;s Tale<br />\n</em><em>Lovecraft Country<br />\n</em><em>The Mandalorian<br />\n</em><em>Pose<br />\n</em><em>This is Us</em></p>\n<p><strong>Outstanding Comedy Series:</strong></p>\n<p><em>Black-ish</em><br />\n<em>Cobra Kai</em><br />\n<em>Emily in Paris</em><br />\n<em>Hacks</em><br />\n<em>The Flight Attendant<br />\nThe Kominsky Method<br />\nPen15<br />\nTed Lasso<br />\n</em></p>\n<p><strong>Outstanding Limited Series:</strong><em><br />\n</em></p>\n<p><em>I May Destroy You</em><br />\n<em>Mare of Easttown</em><br />\n<em>The Queen&#8217;s Gambit</em><br />\n<em>The Underground Railroad</em><br />\n<em>WandaVision</em></p>\n<p><strong>Outstanding TV Movie:</strong></p>\n<p><em>Dolly Parton&#8217;s Christmas on the Square<br />\n</em><em>Oslo<br />\n</em><em>Robin Roberts Presents: Mahalia<br />\n</em><em>Sylvie&#8217;s Love<br />\n</em><em>Uncle Frank</em></p>\n<p><strong>Outstanding Lead Actor in a Drama Series:</strong></p>\n<p>Sterling K. Widow</em></strong> features a post-credits scene that sets the stage for an upcoming Marvel Studios project. However, writer <strong>Eric Pearson</strong> explained that the traditional tag at the end of the credits was almost much different and much longer. In order to dive into the details, we&#8217;ll have to dig into spoiler territory, so if you haven&#8217;t seen <em>Black Widow</em>, then this is your last chance to flee.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Spoilers </strong>for </em>Black Widow <em>follow</em>.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683288\"></span></p>\n<p>We&#8217;ve <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/black-widow-credits-scene-explained/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">already taken a deep dive</a> into the <em>Black Widow</em> credits scene and what it means for the future of the Marvel Cinematic Universe. The biggest takeaway is that Yelena Bolova (<strong>Florence Pugh</strong>) is working for Contessa Valentina Allegra de la Fontaine (<strong>Julia Louis-Dreyfus</strong>), <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-falcon-and-the-winter-soldier-cameo-explained/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a mysterious character</a> introduced in <em>The Falcon and The Winter Soldier</em>. Though their exchange is briefly humorous before setting up a mission of revenge when Yelena is told that Hawkeye is &#8220;responsible&#8221; for Natasha Romanoff&#8217;s death, the scene was first written to be much longer and more playful.</p>\n<p>Writer Eric Pearson recently spoke to <a href=\"https://collider.com/black-widow-post-credits-scene-explained-julia-louis-dreyfus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Collider</a> about how the <em>Black Widow</em> credits scene came together, which was originally meant to mark the introduction of this character when the movie was scheduled to debut in theaters before any of Marvel&#8217;s Disney+ shows premiered. Pearson explained:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;I just know that they told me we have plans to introduce this character Valentina, and it&#8217;s going to be played by Julia Louis Dreyfus. And I couldn&#8217;t get to the computer fast enough.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>It sounds like Pearson wasn&#8217;t really given many details about Val, but he was still able to craft the scene with her personality. Pearson was so excited about how Val would clash with Yelena, who has plenty of funny banter with Natasha in the movie. Pearson recalled:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;That tag scene was probably like five pages long because I was just so greedy. I was like, I want Yelena and Valentina just back and forth, bouncing dialogue off of each other. And ultimately that&#8217;s never going to happen. You&#8217;re not going to have a full scene as a stinger at the end. So we went with the smaller version, but I was just so excited to get those two actors together, to get those two character dynamics together. And I also love taking an emotional moment, like Yelena at the grave, and then flushing it down the toilet with Valentina blowing her nose.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-682044\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/falconandwintersoldier-contessa-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"The Falcon and The Winter Solder - Julia Louis-Dreyfus as Contessa Valentina Allegra de Fontaine\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/falconandwintersoldier-contessa.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/falconandwintersoldier-contessa-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>More Val, Please</h2>\n<p>From what we&#8217;ve seen of Val so far, she&#8217;s extremely nonchalant about pretty much everything. There&#8217;s no room for sentimentality, and she doesn&#8217;t take anything very seriously, even if there are high stakes. Between her conversations with John Walker (<strong>Wyatt Russell</strong>) and Yelena Bolova, it&#8217;s clear Julia Louis-Dreyfus brings a casual attitude to the Marvel Cinematic Universe. But at some point, we&#8217;re hoping there&#8217;s a turn where we get to see how deadly serious she can be when it&#8217;s called for. Because a character like Val doesn&#8217;t hire people like John Walker and Yelena Bolova if she isn&#8217;t up to some nefarious shit.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;re not sure when we&#8217;ll see Contessa Valentina Allegra de la Fontaine again, but a safe bet would probably be in the <em>Hawkeye</em> series, which is slated to arrive sometime later this year.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/extended-black-widow-credits-scene/\">The &#8216;Black Widow&#8217; Post-Credits Scene Was Almost Very Different</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=kmcZntpP-KA:O6CDGdXrf3c:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"Walt Disney World’s Christmas Plans Are Here, and They’re Mostly Spectacular","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683222","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683226 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/tlh029385029834029348234-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/tlh029385029834029348234.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/tlh029385029834029348234-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>It’s Christmas in July, as the saying goes, and that means it’s a perfect time of year to wish it was the actual holiday season. Luckily enough, even though they just recently announced details of how they’ll celebrate Halloween, the <strong>Walt Disney World Resort</strong> is revealing some important details about the first post-pandemic holiday season. It’s not quite as extravagant as in the past, but after 2020, anything is better than nothing.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683222\"></span></p>\n<p>Even as Disney eases into a new normal, there are some changes to report. As the Disney Parks Blog <a href=\"https://disneyparks.disney.go.com/blog/2021/07/the-holiday-season-returns-to-walt-disney-world-resort/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced</a>, <strong>Mickey’s Very Merry Christmas Party</strong> isn’t coming back this year, nor is the Candlelight Processional event. But in their place, we’ll get <strong>Disney Very Merriest After Hours</strong> (a title that presumes the event is somehow better than the Christmas Party, which had the temerity and sheer audacity to only be “very merry,” not “very merriest”) along with <strong>Minnie’s Wonderful Christmastime Fireworks</strong>.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683237\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-magic-kingdom-park-e1626180441236-700x299.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-magic-kingdom-park-e1626180441236-700x300.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-magic-kingdom-park-e1626180441236-360x154.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-magic-kingdom-park-e1626180441236-768x328.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/disney-magic-kingdom-park-e1626180441236.jpeg 900w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Disney&#8217;s Very Merriest After Hours</h2>\n<p>Disney Very Merriest After Hours, aside from being a bit of a mouthful to say or type, is a new hard-ticket event (as ever, yes, that does mean you will have to buy a separate ticket from the basic admission), is a new way to enjoy the Magic Kingdom at the holiday season. The event won’t just feature those fireworks, but plenty of holiday decor and treats, as well as decked-out characters. Over at Disney’s <strong>Hollywood Studios</strong>, Sunset Seasons Greetings returns to offer guests plenty of holiday lights and theming. This event also allows you to see the Hollywood Tower Hotel turned into, among other locations, a Dickensian village inspired by <strong><i>Mickey’s Christmas Carol</i></strong> and the land of Arendelle from <strong><em>Frozen</em></strong>, which is&#8230;well, it’s going to be an interesting use of the Hollywood Tower Hotel, that much is sure.</p>\n<p>Plus all of this, there will be special celebrations at Disney’s Animal Kingdom, the International Festival of the Holidays returning to Epcot throughout the month of December, and plenty of ways to celebrate the season at the Disney hotels and Disney Springs.</p>\n<p>Tickets for the Disney Very Merriest After Hours event will be available next month, but you can take heart for now: Walt Disney World is gearing up for as full-throated a return as possible to the holiday season for <strong>2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/walt-disney-world-christmas-plans/\">Walt Disney World&#8217;s Christmas Plans Are Here, and They&#8217;re Mostly Spectacular</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div But the back finds Luca and Alberto strolling through <span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-poiln3 r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">Portorosso</span> as Giulia passes by with a basket of fish.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683279 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/luca-steelbook-inside-700x666.jpg\" alt=\"Luca Steelbook\" width=\"700\" height=\"666\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/luca-steelbook-inside.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/luca-steelbook-inside-360x343.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Meanwhile, the inside has Luca and Alberto admiring all the work they put into their makeshift Vespa scooter that will inevitably get launched into the ocean. They&#8217;re so proud of their creation! As for the discs, one features all three of our friends on a real Vespa scooter while the other has Luca and Alberto embracing each other as friends while Machiavelli looks on suspiciously.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;re a little surprised the full &#8220;sea monster&#8221; versions of Luca and Alberto aren&#8217;t used more prominently somewhere in the artwork, but our characters spend most of the movie in human form, so I suppose that makes sense. It would be nice if they got a little bit of the spotlight though.</p>\n<p>Get a look at the full list of special features that will be included on the home video release of <em>Luca </em>below.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683281 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/luca-steelbook-front-700x773.jpg\" alt=\"Luca Steelbook\" width=\"700\" height=\"773\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/luca-steelbook-front.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/luca-steelbook-front-360x398.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2 dir=\"auto\">Pixar&#8217;s Luca Special Features</h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Our Italian Inspiration – Experience the joy of discovery as Pixar artists travel to Cinque Terre, Italy, to absorb the beauty and culture of the coastal region which inspired the characters and the quintessential Italian backdrop of “Luca.”</li>\n<li>Secretly A Sea Monster – Explore the artistry and technical innovation of Luca’s transformation from sea monster to human, and how the theme of transformation is central to the emotional journey of the main characters.</li>\n<li>Best Friends – Best friends can challenge us, inspire us, annoy us, and encourage us. The cast and crew of “Luca” share their own stories about how besties influenced their lives, and how those experiences informed the creation of screen pals Luca, Alberto and Giulia.</li>\n<li>Deleted Scenes\n<ul>\n<li>Introduction – Director Enrico Casarosa introduces scenes not included in the final version of “Luca.”</li>\n<li>Starfish Hunt (Alternate Opening) – Luca explores the shore and the sea, gathering mussels and starfish, in this serene alternate opening to the film.</li>\n<li>Isola Del Mare (Alternate Opening) – Luca welcomes viewers to the quiet island he calls home.</li>\n<li>Festa Del Mare – The boys go to a festival filled with fun … and danger.</li>\n<li>Here Comes Giulia – Giulia explores Isola Del Mare, where she meets Luca and Alberto, and asks so many questions.</li>\n<li>Gelato Trouble – Giulia offers to treat Luca and Alberto to something called “gelato.”</li>\n<li>Sea Monster Cannery – Luca dreams about a magical place filled with Vespas and gelato, but things aren’t quite what they seem.</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/luca-steelbook-at-best-buy/\">Exclusive: Get a Look at Series","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683256","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-directors.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683269\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-directors-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"peacemaker directors\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-directors-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-directors-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-directors-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-directors.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong><em>Peacemaker</em></strong>, the<em> Suicide Squad</em> spin-off headed to HBO Max, has wrapped filming – and this news comes with info on who will be directing the series. We already knew that <em>The Suicide Squad</em> filmmaker <strong>James Gunn</strong> directed five of the show&#8217;s eight episodes, and now we know who will be sharing directorial duties. That small list that includes <strong>Jody Hill</strong> (<em>Observe and Report</em>), <strong>Brad Anderson</strong> (<em>Session 9</em>), and <strong>Rosemary Rodriguez</strong> (<em>Jessica Jones</em>).</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683256\"></span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/john-cena-peaccemaker-suicide-squade-first-look.jpeg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683268\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/john-cena-peaccemaker-suicide-squade-first-look-700x394.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"394\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/john-cena-peaccemaker-suicide-squade-first-look-700x394.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/john-cena-peaccemaker-suicide-squade-first-look-360x203.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/john-cena-peaccemaker-suicide-squade-first-look-768x432.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/john-cena-peaccemaker-suicide-squade-first-look.jpeg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Peacemaker Wraps Filming</strong></h2>\n<p>James Gunn took to Twitter to reveal that filming on <em>Peacemaker</em>, the upcoming <em>The Suicide Squad</em> spinoff series starring <strong>John Cen</strong>a, has wrapped. &#8220;<span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-poiln3 r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">Less than a year ago I pitched a vague pitch to HBO Max –</span><span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-poiln3 r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\"> here we are 11 months later with 8 astounding episodes in the can. Cast &#38; crew: I love you all. Thank you for putting your hearts &#38; souls into this project,&#8221; Gunn <a href=\"https://twitter.com/JamesGunn/status/1414783283653718016\">wrote</a>. </span></p>\n<p>The series &#8220;will explore the origins of the character that Cena will play in the upcoming film, a man who believes in peace at any cost — no matter how many people he has to kill to get it. The series will extend the world that Gunn is creating for <em>The Suicide Squad</em> movie, which is scheduled to be released in theaters by Warner Bros. Pictures on August 6, 2021.&#8221;</p>\n<p>While a show that explores the origins of a character sounds like a prequel, we still don&#8217;t know how this will all play out. Part of the mystery is because we don&#8217;t know if Cena&#8217;s Peacemaker lives through <em>The Suicide Squad</em>. &#8220;<em>Peacemaker</em> is an opportunity to delve into current world issues through the lens of this superhero/supervillain/and world’s biggest douchebag,&#8221; James Gunn said when the show was announced. &#8220;I’m excited to expand <em>The Suicide Squad</em> and bring this character from the DC film universe to the full breadth of a series. And of course, to be able to work again with John, Peter, and my friends at Warner Bros. is the icing on the cake.&#8221;</p>\n<p>John Cena added: &#8220;I have said before that it has been a tremendous honor and an incredible opportunity to be part of <em>The Suicide Squad</em> and to work with James on what is going to be a fantastic movie. I am unbelievably excited to have the chance to team up with him again for <em>Peacemaker</em>. We can’t wait for fans to see this.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-e1604067342820.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-643696\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-e1604067342820-700x320.jpg\" alt=\"peacemaker cast\" width=\"700\" height=\"320\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-e1604067342820-700x320.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-e1604067342820-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-e1604067342820-768x351.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-e1604067342820.jpg 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Peacemaker Directors</strong></h2>\n<p>The news that <em>Peacemaker</em> has wrapped also comes with info on the show&#8217;s directors. Gunn confirmed that Jody Hill, the filmmaker behind <em>Observe and Report</em>, <em>Eastbound &#38; Down</em>, <em>Vice Principals</em>, and <em>The Righteous Gemstones</em><em>, </em>was one of the directors on the show. On Twitter, Gunn <a href=\"https://twitter.com/JamesGunn/status/1414022906699526144\">said</a>: &#8220;I&#8217;ve known Jody a long time. I love <em>Observe &#38; Report</em> and <em>Foot Fist Way</em> and early on an exec at HBO Max described <em>Peacemaker</em> as <em>Eastbound &#38; Down</em> meets <em>Watchmen</em> so I thought I’d go directly to the source. Loved having him involved.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, <a href=\"https://collider.com/peacemaker-directors-james-gunn-jody-hill-brad-anderson-rosemary-rodriguez/\">Collider</a> has confirmed that  Brad Anderson and Rosemary Rodriguez are also directors on the show. Anderson&#8217;s credits include the excellent indie horror movies <em>Session 9</em> and <em>The Machinist</em>, while Rodriguez has helmed episodes of <em>Jessica Jones</em>, <em>Dickinson</em>, <em>The Walking Dead</em>, and more. <em>Peacemaker</em> is set to arrive on HBO Max in <strong>January 2022</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/peacemaker-directors/\">&#8216;Peacemaker&#8217; Wraps Filming on Season 1, James Gunn Reveals Directors for HBO Max Series</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\"
