14:54:16 +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-directors-700x321.jpg","linkMd5":"4d7ba4057b7cf47e09c8805fe4074a8d","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn32@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-02-487_18e272daf9c4b958.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":321,"sourceBytes":23702,"destBytes":14862,"author":"Chris Evangelista","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-directors-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn32@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-02-487_18e272daf9c4b958.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/john-cena-peaccemaker-suicide-squade-first-look-700x394.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn66@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-13-952_5e0ee9787489cc49.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/peacemaker-e1604067342820-700x320.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn95@2020_6/2021/07/13/17-22-14-026_226a8e67ee5c6830.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn76@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-14-413_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=3dQca-OgLSA:yyiV6lNWmfg:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn83@2020_5/2021/07/13/17-22-13-957_1a5feb741632462a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn3@2020_1/2021/07/13/17-22-14-788_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=3dQca-OgLSA:yyiV6lNWmfg:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn91@2020_4/2021/07/13/17-22-14-348_e174672a6ba26b81.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/3dQca-OgLSA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn3@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-24-332_6d2f54412c3a2916.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626196915176},{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"‘Gunpowder Milkshake’ Review: A ‘John Wick’ Wannabe That’s Never as Cool as It Thinks It Is","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683223","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683228 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Karen-and-Chloe-GPM-5.11-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Karen-and-Chloe-GPM-5.11.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Karen-and-Chloe-GPM-5.11-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>The impressive success of the <i>John Wick</i> films is much like the success of any franchise – if one studio has achieved it, another wants to duplicate it. So the existence of <strong><i>Gunpowder Milkshake</i></strong>, a new Netflix action film that feels reverse-engineered to draw in enough viewers to inspire at least one or two follow-up entries, is only surprising because it took so long for a studio to nakedly try to create its own John Wick.</p>\n<p>But as the old saying goes, a child prodigy may know the notes, but they still don’t know the music. <i>Gunpowder Milkshake</i> broadly tiptoes around what made <i>John Wick</i> work, but does so in a glib and hollow fashion. There’s a lot of flash and style, and all in service of an empty story with unmemorable gunplay.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683223\"></span></p>\n<p><strong>Karen Gillan</strong> stars as Sam, a single-minded young assassin who works for a shadowy group called The Firm, which is made up of a lot of old white men in suits who control&#8230;well, to hear her tell it, they control everything. She’s watched over by Nathan (<strong>Paul Giamatti</strong>), a kindly member of the Firm’s HR group, which basically means he’s the guy who tells her who to kill, where, and when. After one job goes a bit pear-shaped, Nathan gives Sam her new assignment: retrieving cash stolen by a Firm accountant who’s in over his head. But that job goes even more pear-shaped: she inadvertently kills the nebbish, leaving behind his unassuming daughter Emily (<strong>Chloe Coleman</strong>). Since Sam herself was left orphaned by her mother (<strong>Lena Headey</strong>) 15 years ago, she gets guilty enough to drag Emily along on the rest of her now bloodier adventure, as she tries to keep the girl safe while killing some more bad guys and coming into contact with friends of her mother’s, all of whom are – like her – secret badass assassins.</p>\n<p>Co-writer and director <strong>Navot Papushado</strong> – best known in the States among indie crowds for directing the thriller <i>Big Bad Wolves</i> – wants very badly for <i>Gunpowder Milkshake</i> to be cool and slick, seemingly as inspired by Quentin Tarantino’s films as by the work of Chad Stahelski and David Leitch in the <i>John Wick</i> movies. (The film’s title is mostly nonsense, but whenever Sam meets up with Nathan, it’s at a 1950s-era diner with a big old-school milkshake with two straws jutting out of the glass.) But the problem is that the harder this movie tries to be cool, the more it struggles to actually <i>be</i> cool. Where <i>Gunpowder Milkshake</i> really stumbles is in trying to depict R-rated violence, replete with CG blood spatter, in a glib and cheeky manner. It’s not enough for Papushado to do a slow-motion tracking shot through the diner as Sam and her mother’s fellow assassins (played by <strong>Angela Bassett</strong>, <strong>Carla Gugino</strong>, and <strong>Michelle Yeoh</strong>) lay waste to handfuls of faceless baddies, but we have to hear an upbeat number on the soundtrack to play off the faux-bloody violence. It&#8217;s tired.</p>\n<p>Papushado, too, doesn’t always stage the action in impressive fashion. It’s nowhere near as incomprehensible as some modern action fare tends to be, but again, in a film inviting comparisons with <i>John Wick</i>, it’s hard to measure up, as much of the action happens all too quickly with jump cuts and rapid-fire editing. The cast is up to the task of the violence, with Gillan (unfortunately saddled with an American accent masking her native Scottish brogue) doing a fine riff on characters like John Wick and the T-800 from <i>T2</i>, as she plays off the blandly precocious Coleman. Headey, Bassett, Gugino, and Yeoh are all fun (though they’re mostly only present in the second half), but playing roles they could do in their sleep.</p>\n<p>That’s frankly how <i>Gunpowder Milkshake</i> feels as a whole – this is a movie that has sprung up out of existence less from creative desire than from a series of checkboxes and an unwieldy blend of past, better action films. Putting together a cast this talented either means that it’ll be somewhat frustrating to watch them stranded in fare that they’re too good for, or that the result will be an energetic blast. Sadly, <i>Gunpowder Milkshake</i> is the former. All of these actors are too good to appear in what ends up being such a rote, uninspired affair. For a studio like Netflix to see the success of <i>John Wick</i> and want to find something like that for themselves is perfectly logical. Who wouldn’t want to create a franchise out of whole cloth like that? But it’s hard enough to capture lightning in a bottle. <i>Gunpowder Milkshake</i> is as if the studio tried to force lightning into a bottle, and only got left with a stray spark or two.</p>\n<p><strong>/Film Rating: 4 out of 10</strong></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/gunpowder-milkshake-review/\">&#8216;Gunpowder Milkshake&#8217; Review: A &#8216;John Wick&#8217; Wannabe That&#8217;s Never as Cool as It Thinks It Is</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Fall","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683036","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-683078 aligncenter\" href=\"https://hasbropulse.com/pages/hasbro-pulse-con-2021\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">is returning this year</a> to reveal a bunch of new toys and collectibles from <em><strong>Star Wars</strong></em>, <strong>Marvel</strong>, <strong><em>Transformers</em></strong>, <strong><em>Power Rangers</em></strong>, <em><strong>G.I. Joe</strong></em>, and more. Though we&#8217;re not sure what the toy makers will be revealing during the virtual event, they&#8217;ve already shown off a batch of<em> Star Wars</em> Hasbro PulseCon 2021 exclusives, such as the debut of <strong><em>The Mandalorian</em></strong> executive producer <strong>Dave Filoni</strong> action figure in the form of X-wing pilot Trapper Wolf. But that&#8217;s not all.<span id=\"more-683036\"></span></p>\n\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/new-star-wars-toys-include-x-wing-pilot-dave-filoni-more-as-hasbro-pulsecon-2021-exclusives-this-fall/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-trapperwolf-box/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-trapperwolf-box-360x360.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"Star Wars Hasbro PulseCon 2021 Exclusives\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-trapperwolf-box-360x360.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-trapperwolf-box.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/new-star-wars-toys-include-x-wing-pilot-dave-filoni-more-as-hasbro-pulsecon-2021-exclusives-this-fall/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-trapperwolf-open/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-trapperwolf-open-360x360.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"Star Wars Hasbro PulseCon 2021 Exclusives\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-trapperwolf-open-360x360.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-trapperwolf-open.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n\n<h2>Star Wars: The Black Series &#8211; Dave Filoni as Trapper Wolf</h2>\n<p><em>The Mandalorian</em> executive producer Dave Filoni entered the live-action <em>Star Wars</em> universe as X-wing pilot Trapper Wolf in the show&#8217;s first season on Disney+. The Rebel was one of a trio of pilots who descend upon the prisoner transport known as Bothan-Five at the end of &#8220;Chapter 6: The Prisoner.&#8221; Trapper Wolf then returned in &#8220;Chapter 10: The Passenger&#8221; alongside Carson Teva, portrayed by Korean Canadian actor Paul Sun-Hyung Lee. They first gave Mando some trouble, causing him to crash land on an ice planet, and then they showed up in the nick of time to help him with some terrifying ice spiders.</p>\n<p>This is the kind of<em> Star Wars</em> action figure that&#8217;s made for the hardcore fans. It&#8217;s also the kind of figure that could make for some fun diorama scenes on shelves. If you take Trapper Wolf&#8217;s head, give it a cowboy hat, and put it on a more generic action 6-inch action figure from Hasbro, perhaps one from Marvel Legends, then you have a Dave Filoni action figure that you can pose to direct scenes from <em>The Mandalorian</em>. We know all the kids are dying to add Dave Filoni to their <em>Star Wars</em> collection.</p>\n\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/new-star-wars-toys-include-x-wing-pilot-dave-filoni-more-as-hasbro-pulsecon-2021-exclusives-this-fall/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-cantinashowdown-box/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-cantinashowdown-box-360x360.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"Star Wars Hasbro PulseCon 2021 Exclusives\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-cantinashowdown-box-360x360.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-cantinashowdown-box.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/new-star-wars-toys-include-x-wing-pilot-dave-filoni-more-as-hasbro-pulsecon-2021-exclusives-this-fall/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-cantinashowdown-open/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-cantinashowdown-open-360x360.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"Star Wars Hasbro PulseCon 2021 Exclusives\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-cantinashowdown-open-360x360.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blackseries-pulsecon2021-cantinashowdown-open.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n\n<h2>Star Wars: The Black Series – Cantina Showdown</h2>\n<p>Longtime fans of <em>Star Wars</em> action figures will recognize the Power of the Force packaging for this latest Black Series playset. The Cantina Showdown was a three-pack of 3.75-inch action figures from Kenner back in 1997, the year the Special Edition releases of the <em>Star Wars</em> trilogy arrived in theaters. Now that same box set inspired by <strong><em>A New Hope</em></strong> is being turned into a bigger 6-inch set.</p>\n<p>The Black Series Cantina Showdown playset comes with Obi-Wan Kenobi, Dr. Evanzan, and Ponda Baba action figures as well as a piece of the Mos Eisley cantina bar. There are no photographs of Ponda Baba with his arm cut off by Obi-Wan Kenobi&#8217;s lightsaber, but if one of his arms isn&#8217;t detachable, then that&#8217;s a real missed opportunity. Get a closer look at the playset <a href=\"https://hasbropulse.com/products/star-wars-the-black-series-the-power-of-the-force-cantina-showdown\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">at Hasbro Pulse</a>.</p>\n\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/new-star-wars-toys-include-x-wing-pilot-dave-filoni-more-as-hasbro-pulsecon-2021-exclusives-this-fall/starwars-blakseries-pulsecon2021-throneroom-box/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blakseries-pulsecon2021-throneroom-box-360x360.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"Star Wars Hasbro PulseCon 2021 Exclusives\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blakseries-pulsecon2021-throneroom-box-360x360.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blakseries-pulsecon2021-throneroom-box.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/new-star-wars-toys-include-x-wing-pilot-dave-filoni-more-as-hasbro-pulsecon-2021-exclusives-this-fall/starwars-blakseries-pulsecon2021-throneroom-open/'><img width=\"360\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blakseries-pulsecon2021-throneroom-open-360x360.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"Star Wars Hasbro PulseCon 2021 Exclusives\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blakseries-pulsecon2021-throneroom-open-360x360.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/starwars-blakseries-pulsecon2021-throneroom-open.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 360px) 100vw, 360px\" /></a>\n\n<h2>Star Wars: The Vintage Collection &#8211; The Emperor&#8217;s Throne Room</h2>\n<p>Finally, for all you collectors out there who have stuck with the smaller scale 3.75-inch action figures all these years, Hasbro is releasing a <strong><em>Return of the Jedi</em></strong> playset for The Vintage Collection.</p>\n<p>Emperor Palpatine&#8217;s throne room from the second Death Star can be added to your collection complete with the iconic window background that looks upon the space battle between Rebel and Imperial pilots. The Emperor&#8217;s Throne Room playset includes Emperor Palpatine in cloth robe with lightning hands, cane, and Luke Skywalker’s lightsaber hilt. There&#8217;s also the throne for him to sit on and cackle endlessly.</p>\n<p>All three of these Star Wars Hasbro PulseCon exclusives <a href=\"https://hasbropulse.com/collections/hasbro-pulse-exclusives\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">will be available at their website</a> to order sometime this fall sometime during Hasbro PulseCon 2021. We don&#8217;t know exactly when that will be yet, but we&#8217;ll be sure to keep you posted.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/new-star-wars-toys-include-x-wing-pilot-dave-filoni-more-as-hasbro-pulsecon-2021-exclusives-this-fall/\">New &#8216;Star Wars&#8217; Toys Include X-Wing Pilot Dave 879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=NJfci1DOnGE:jt4l00z9rt0:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn3@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-14-036_24f8d0495c7eb641.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/NJfci1DOnGE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn28@2020_2/2021/07/13/17-22-14-030_bee95f6d4f5e2ec4.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626196915176},{"createdTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"‘Benedetta’ Review: Paul Verhoeven’s Lesbian Nun Drama Toes the Line Between Profound and Profane [Cannes]","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683239","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-683240\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/benedetta-e1626181027566-700x299.jpeg\" alt=\"benedetta review\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/benedetta-e1626181027566-700x300.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/benedetta-e1626181027566-360x154.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/benedetta-e1626181027566-768x328.jpeg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong><em>Benedetta</em></strong> begins with a minor miracle, when a young girl en route to enter a convent prays at an altar to the Virgin Mary to dissuade a bandit from attacking her family. A bird flies out and defecates in the one unscarred eye of the would-be attacker, thus setting the stage of a film that itself is a minor miracle, one that also pairs the glory of religious expression with the everyday navigation of shit being flung.</p>\n<p>Based on an academic tome by Judith Brown published in 1986 that provided exacting detail drawn from the 17th century court proceedings, <strong>Paul Verhoeven</strong> and his <em>Elle</em> screenwriting collaborator <strong>David Birke</strong> have moulded this story of lesbian love, political corruption, and plague-era mischief into a work of salacious brilliance.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683239\"></span></p>\n<p>Anchored by extraordinary performances by <strong>Virginie Efira</strong>, <strong>Daphne Patakia</strong>, <strong>Lambert Wilson</strong>, and the international treasure that is <strong>Charlotte Rampling</strong>, at its core the film is about the mechanism of lying and its underpinning of faith and belief, and the existential crisis that occurs when one encounters a confabulator even more capable of mass delusion, both regarding untruths told to others and especially the lies told unto themselves.</p>\n<p>This is a deeply nihilistic narrative, one that on its surface lays bare the raw political machinations supposedly done for higher purposes. An opening scene where a barter for the rate of dowry exhibits the collision between the pragmatic and the guise of ethical superiority, and from there the story exposes how the very institutions themselves corrupt any notion of purity of spirit.</p>\n<p>Along the way the two leads engage in congress in a way that’s equal parts erotic, engaging, preposterous, and profound. The humor at play is as dark as the plague. There are twin devices that are vaginally inserted that are two sides of the coin – one for pleasure, one for torture – but each in fundamental ways iconic talismans of the church’s power to shape behavior.</p>\n<p>As the violence escalates, the lies become more and more sophisticated, resulting in a Shakespearean battle of wills that upsets the direct balance of power within the convent. It’s only when the wall is breached that the true evil is let in, and the internecine battles between the nuns made more insignificant by the larger institutions that hold even greater power. Throughout we meet those who espouse faith while holding little belief in higher powers themselves, parsing evidentiary elements of supposed miracles, or being skeptical that the convenient excuses of religious epiphany appear identical to the ravings of lunacy.</p>\n<p>Shot with a cool touch, the film looks like some lost tapestry, with candle-lit cells and dreary convent walls speaking of the insular nature of the nuns. Even in the broad daylight there’s a muddy palor, yet the spark connecting Benedetta to her lover glows as bright as the sun.</p>\n<p>This is another in Verhoeven’s long career of films that manage to be satiric, provocative, banal and bravura simultaneously, with several fart jokes littered amongst dialogue scenes that are presented with a chilly formalism. The web of connections between the characters, particularly the nuns, exhibit a cloistered, claustrophobic dread, even when moments of intimacy are allowed to shine.</p>\n<p>This is a film unafraid to be soiled, unabashed to lay bare the truths of the lies and the hypocrisies of the hyperbolically chaste. The result in a film where the most just must be sacrificed and the most corrupt allowed to rise implausibly to power, all under the guise of an invisible being supposedly controlling even the most wicked of acts.</p>\n<p>Verhoeven made clear that this cannot be blasphemy, for it is based on what really happened. Whether that logic stands is up for debate, but what’s not is that this is a tonally rich, libidinously powerful, and psychologically complex tale told by a master filmmaker equally at ease with European art-film conventions and B-movie hijinks. It’s this exceptional balance between the profane and the profound that sets <em>Benedetta</em> apart, truly proving to be penetrating in its effect in more ways than one.</p>\n<p><strong>/Film Rating: 8.5 out of 10</strong></p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/benedetta-review-cannes/\">&#8216;Benedetta&#8217; Review: Paul Verhoeven&#8217;s Lesbian Nun Drama Toes the Line Between Profound and Profane [Cannes]</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Yourself","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=683336","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-612810 aligncenter\" https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/dune-1-e1586869122650-768x346.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>It’s been a hot minute since Warner Bros. released any The world of Dune is hot…in more ways than one. Yes, I’m talking about the cast. Today, IMAX announced that their theaters will have their own special <em>Dune </em>content, descriptively titled <em><a href=\"https://imaxexclusive.dunemovie.com/\">IMAX Presents: An Exclusive Look at Dune</a></em>.  The viewings take place July 21 and 22 and will have never-before-seen <em>Dune </em>footage and will culminate with the dropping of a new trailer.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683336\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>Your Destiny Awaits…At IMAX?</strong></h2>\n<p>Need a lil’ extra <em>Dune</em>-ness to get you hyped before you head to an IMAX theater? The official <em>Dune </em>Twitter account has got you covered:</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">YOUR DESTINY AWAITS. <a href=\"https://twitter.com/IMAX?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@IMAX</a> presents: An Exclusive Look at DUNE featuring never-before-seen footage, music and a first look at the New Trailer. Reserve your seats NOW: <a href=\"https://t.co/IRn1Ta5mtp\">https://t.co/IRn1Ta5mtp</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/iriDdfsntX\">pic.twitter.com/iriDdfsntX</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; DUNE (@dunemovie) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dunemovie/status/1414962951891587089?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 13, 2021</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>Granted, what footage is in that clip is also in the first trailer, but it still gets the heart racing! There aren’t specifics of what extra, exclusive footage IMAX theater-goers will get. All IMAX is telling us so far is that there will be &#8220;never-before-seen footage, music from the film, and more.&#8221; And, of course, that new trailer!</p>\n<p>I’m very excited for Villeneuve’s <em>Dune</em> movie. I’m a big fan of the books (and less of a fan of other adaptations), and everything in first trailer looks amazing: The cast! The landscape! That sandworm! The trailer also makes clear that the film is one made for theaters (and, dare I say it, an IMAX screen).  Warner Bros. and IMAX no doubt think the same, which is why we likely have this exclusive IMAX offering in the first place.</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-622766 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/dune-footage-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"dune footage\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/dune-footage-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/dune-footage-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/dune-footage-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/dune-footage.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2><strong>That Smokin’ <em>Dune</em> Cast</strong></h2>\n<p>Remember when I said <em>Dune</em>’s cast was very attractive? Here’s the proof. <em>Dune</em>’s cast includes <strong>Timothée Chalamet</strong> as Paul Atreides; <strong>Rebecca Ferguson</strong> as Lady Jessica; <strong>Oscar Isaac</strong> as Duke Leto Atreides; <strong>Josh Brolin</strong> as Gurney Halleck; <strong>Stellan Skarsgård</strong> as Baron Vladimir Harkonnen; <strong>Dave Bautista</strong> as Glossu Rabban; <strong>Stephen McKinley Henderson</strong> as Thufir Hawat; <strong>Zendaya</strong> as Chani; <strong>David Dastmalchian</strong> as Piter De Vries; <strong>Chang Chen</strong> as Dr. Wellington Yueh; <strong>Sharon Duncan-Brewster</strong> as Dr. Liet-Kynes<strong>; Charlotte Rampling</strong> as Gaius Helen Mohiam<strong>; Jason Momoa</strong> as Duncan Idaho; and <strong>Javier Bardem</strong> as Stilgar.</p>\n<p><em>IMAX Presents: An Exclusive Look at Dune</em> will be in IMAX theaters <strong>July 21 and 22</strong>. You can buy tickets to the event <a href=\"https://www.dunemovie.com/\">here</a>.</p>\n<p><em>Dune</em>, the movie, is set to premiere in theaters and HBO Max on <strong>October 1, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/new-dune-trailer-and-footage-imax-theaters/\">New &#8216;Dune&#8217; Trailer and Footage Coming to IMAX Theaters – 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"Scream: Release Date, Cast and More","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682204","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-646339 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/scream-5-e1605710973270-700x364.jpeg\" alt=\"scream 5 filming\" width=\"700\" height=\"364\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/scream-5-e1605710973270-700x364.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/scream-5-e1605710973270-360x187.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/scream-5-e1605710973270-768x399.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/scream-5-e1605710973270.jpeg 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><em>(Welcome to …And More, our no-frills, zero B.S. guide to when and where you can watch upcoming movies and shows, and everything else you could possibly stand to know.)</em></p>\n<p>Someone has taken their love of scary movies decades too far… that’s right, Ghostface is returning to Woodsboro and we’re all going with him! Next year, the <em><strong>Scream</strong></em> franchise makes a comeback with its highly-anticipated fifth movie. Here’s everything you need to know before the latest slasher hits theaters.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682204\"></span></p>\n<h2>Scream Release Date and Where You Can Watch It</h2>\n<p>Production on <em>Scream</em>, or <em><strong>Scream 5</strong></em> as we&#8217;ll call it, was set to begin back in May 2020, before being delayed due to pandemic complications. Thankfully, filming was safely underway by September and officially wrapped that November. With production finally concluded as of July, the film is currently scheduled for release on <strong>January 14, 2022</strong>.</p>\n<p>It’s a bit of a wait but apparently, many precautions have been taken to assure nothing leaks before the film&#8217;s official release. We previously <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/new-scream-movie-multiple-versions-spoilers/\">reported</a> that there are multiple versions of the screenplay and alternate endings shot to help hide all the set secrets.</p>\n<h2>What is Scream 5?</h2>\n<p>Back in 1996, legendary director <strong>Wes Craven</strong> revitalized horror movies with his witty slasher flick, <strong><em>Scream</em></strong>. It took notes from the many famous slashers and horror movies of the past, using their trends and formulas to wink at the audience and make fun while causing terror. The film followed teenager Sydney Prescott (<strong>Neve Campbell</strong>) and its three sequels continued to torture her into adulthood. She’s stalked by the masked and mysterious Ghostface, a mysterious killer that murders those around her, in an effort to kill Sydney herself or simply torment her with their deaths.</p>\n<p>In the fourth film, Sydney returns to Westboro and reconnects with friends that survived the Ghostface attacks of the past. But her return inspires yet another masked killer, donning the iconic Ghostface mask. Things go as usual: everyone in danger, a killer on the loose, a series of attempts to discover who it is, and the final unmasking of Ghostface. And plenty of blood spilled along the way.</p>\n<h2>Is Scream 5 a Sequel or a Reboot?</h2>\n<p>Here’s where things get interesting: this latest installment in the franchise presently titled <em>Scream</em>, with no number attached. Though it&#8217;s billed as a reboot, it&#8217;s also a direct sequel to <em><strong>Scream 4</strong></em>, a film that followed the events of the trilogy but also added a new cast of teenagers to join the familiar cast of adults. <em>Scream 5</em> is expected to take a similar approach.</p>\n<h2>Scream Synopsis</h2>\n<p>Few details have been revealed about the specific story of <em>Scream 5</em>, but here’s the synopsis.</p>\n<blockquote><p>A new installment of the &#8216;Scream&#8217; horror franchise will follow a woman returning to her home town to try to find out who has been committing a series of vicious crimes.</p></blockquote>\n<h2>Scream Cast</h2>\n<p><em>Scream 5</em> sees the return of the beloved final girl and star of the previous films, <strong>Neve Campbell</strong> as Sydney Prescott. Also reprising their roles are <strong>David Arquette</strong>, <strong>Courtney Cox</strong>, <strong>Roger L. Jackson</strong>, and <strong>Marley Shelton</strong>. Westboro newcomers include <strong>Melissa Barrera</strong> (<strong><em>In the Heights</em></strong>), <strong>Jenna Ortega</strong> (<strong><em>The Fallout</em></strong>), <strong>Mason Gooding</strong> (<em><strong>Love Victor</strong></em>), and <strong>Dylan Minnette</strong> (<em><strong>13 Reasons Why</strong></em>) likely playing the latest teenage targets of Ghostface.</p>\n<h2>Scream Director, Crew, and More</h2>\n<p>Sadly, <em>Scream 5</em> is the first in the franchise not to be directed by Wes Craven, who passed in 2015. But the film still has an impressive team behind it, with filmmakers who understand the weight of the franchise legacy. This includes the directing team of <strong>Matt Bettinelli-Olpin</strong> and <strong>Tyler Gillett, </strong>who previously worked on the 2012 anthology film <em><strong>V/H/S</strong></em> and more recently, 2019&#8217;s <em><strong>Ready or Not</strong></em>. The latter film was a pleasant and bloody surprise, blending horror, black comedy, and satire just as the <em>Scream</em> franchise before it.</p>\n<p><em>Scream 5</em> is written and produced by James Vanderbilt, the writer behind <em>Ready or Not</em> and <strong>David Fincher</strong>&#8216;s 2007 thriller <em><strong>Zodiac</strong></em>. <strong>Paul Neinstein</strong>, <strong>Chad Villella,</strong> and <strong>William Sherak</strong> are set to produce. The score will be handled by <strong>Brian Tyler</strong> (<strong><em>Fast &#38; Furious</em></strong>, <em>Ready or Not</em>, <em><strong>Escape Room</strong></em>).</p>\n<h2>Scream Teaser</h2>\n<p>We have yet to see a trailer or any real footage from the film, but director <strong>Matt Bettinelli-Olpin</strong> recently tweeted a photo celebrating the completion of the film.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-681597 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Scream-5-700x525.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"525\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Scream-5-700x525.png 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Scream-5-360x270.png 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Scream-5-768x576.png 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Scream-5.png 1262w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>With production now completed, hopefully, an actual peek at the film is soon to follow.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/scream-release-date-cast-and-more/\">Scream: 01:21:55","updatedTime":"2021-07-14 01:21:55","title":"The Future of /Film: A Long-Awaited Redesign, a Newly Expanded Writing Staff, and Saying Farewell to an Old Friend","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=682787","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-682835 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/SlashFilm-Logo-700x233.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"233\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/SlashFilm-Logo-700x233.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/SlashFilm-Logo-360x120.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/SlashFilm-Logo-768x256.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/SlashFilm-Logo.jpeg 1500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Change is hard. Change is exciting. Change is an opportunity for us to break out any number of cliches to talk about change, because it can be ecstatic and painful and bittersweet and thrilling. This is especially true when it comes to the places you love – including the movie websites you visit on a regular basis.</p>\n<p><strong>/Film</strong> is in the midst of its biggest change since it was founded back in 2005. And we get it. Change is weird. But it&#8217;s also exciting. Lots of things are changing for this website right now, both behind the scenes and on the front page, but this is our promise to you: /Film will always be /Film, your smart, honest, enthusiastic, occasionally a bit snarky (but never cruel) source for all things movie, television, and pop culture. We&#8217;re not going anywhere, even as we welcome a brand new look and a bunch of new faces, and as we say goodbye to one of our oldest friends.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s what lies ahead for /Film in the weeks and months ahead.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-682787\"></span></p>\n<h2>A Total Site Redesign</h2>\n<p>When I first joined /Film back in 2015 (was it really that long ago?), there were already discussions of when and how to redesign the site. But today, we can reveal that the site is finally getting the overhaul it deserves.</p>\n<p>In the very near future (exact date to be determined), /Film will relaunch with a spiffy new design that will do away with our current look entirely and change the way you read and enjoy the site. The desktop redesign will launch simultaneously with a new mobile site. In addition to aesthetics, the new design will load much faster, and it will be easier to navigate and find articles as they are published. It&#8217;s a total overhaul, and one that will benefit everyone.</p>\n<p>However, the writing will still be /Film through and through. But now, it&#8217;ll be presented in a shiny and modern package, and we can&#8217;t wait for you to see it.</p>\n<h2>The Comments Section is Going Away</h2>\n<p>There is one element of the redesign that we understand will be controversial: the comments section will no longer exist in the relaunched /Film. This was a major point of conversation for the team, as we understand many friendships were formed in our comments section over the years. So if you have any internet friends you want to stay in touch with, please use the comments section under this article to let your fellow commenters know where they can find you, and arrange ways to stay in touch after the relaunch.</p>\n<p>If you want to remain an active member of the /Film community, our social media feeds are currently undergoing a major overhaul and are ready for your participation, but we&#8217;ll talk about that in a moment.</p>\n<h2>The Writers You Enjoy Aren&#8217;t Going Anywhere</h2>\n<p>Even as things change, plenty will remain the same&#8230;even though everyone has new titles. /Film founder <strong>Peter Sciretta</strong> is now editorial director, and I am now senior news editor. We&#8217;re still doing a lot of the old things – but also a lot of new things, too.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, the core crew is more active than ever. <strong>Hoai-Tran Bui</strong> has accepted a promotion to news editor, while <strong>Bradford Oman </strong>(AKA <strong>Ethan Anderton</strong>) and <strong>Chris Evangelista</strong> have joined <strong>Ben Pearson</strong> as senior writers. Chris has also taken on the title of chief film critic. All titles reflect what they have brought to the site over the years and how they will continue to lead the charge in how /Film reads and sounds, even as our look changes.</p>\n<h2>There Are a Bunch of New Names on the News Staff</h2>\n<p>If you&#8217;re a regular reader, you may have noticed a number of new names contributing on a regular basis. That&#8217;s because, in addition to our regular contributors and columnists (who also aren&#8217;t going anywhere), we have expanded our news desk with names both new and familiar to /Film.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;d like to officially welcome <strong>Jeremy Mathai</strong>, <strong>Shania Russell</strong>, <strong>Danielle Ryan</strong>, <strong>Vanessa Armstrong</strong>, <strong>Joshua Meyer</strong>, <strong>Marisa Mirabal</strong>, and <strong>Eric Vespe</strong> to the /Film news desk. What this means is, well, <em>more</em>. More news articles on a daily basis, more articles during the evenings and weekends, more deep-dives into your latest obsessions, and more feature writing in general.</p>\n<p>In addition, <strong>Chris Gates</strong> is our new features editor, overseeing a new section of the site focused on lists and longform posts. <strong>Ariel Fisher</strong> has joined the site as our evening editor, taking care of late-breaking news after the daytime crew has shuffled home. We have also handed theme park coverage over to regular contributor <strong>Josh Spiegel</strong>, who has transformed the Theme Park Bits column into an ongoing beat.</p>\n<p>As /Film heads into its next generation, having a passionate, diverse, and talented staff of writers of all tastes and backgrounds remains vital. This is just the beginning, and we hope you enjoy reading them as much as we do.</p>\n<h2>Our Social Media is Receiving an Overhaul</h2>\n<p>If you read /Film but don&#8217;t follow us on social media, this is the perfect time to start. Our <a href=\"https://twitter.com/slashfilm\">Twitter feed</a> has been overhauled and now acts as the feed for the site itself (it stopped being Peter&#8217;s personal feed a little while back, but you can still follow him <a href=\"https://twitter.com/PeterSciretta\">here</a>). Twitter is still one of the best places to track new /Film articles, but it will now include updates on movie and TV news not covered in full posts, as well as cool movie trivia and looks back at some of our favorite moments in cinema history. Our goal is for it to be a feed that entertains as much as it offers links to our stories.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, the changes continue to our <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/slashfilm\">Facebook page</a>, and our brand new <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/slashfilm/\">Instagram page</a> is just waiting for /Film readers to start following it.</p>\n<h2>The Future of Podcasts on /Film</h2>\n<p>And now we get to the bittersweet part. As you may have <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-slashfilmcast-is-now-the-filmcast-heres-what-you-need-to-know/\">already seen in a previous post written by <strong>David Chen</strong></a>, <strong>The Slashfilmcast</strong> is rebranding to <strong>The Filmcast</strong> and is parting ways with /Film. There is no bad blood here and we remain great friends with that crew – this is an amicable separation and we expect to continue collaborating in the future. You will even hear /Film writers still guesting on The Filmcast! That post linked above will have the in-depth answers you need, but the podcast will keep on moving without a hitch, just as its own independent entity.</p>\n<p>However, the <strong>/Film Daily</strong> podcast is not going anywhere, and will continue to arrive every weekday, with the same regular cast.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-future-of-film-a-long-awaited-redesign-a-newly-expanded-writing-staff-and-saying-farewell-to-an-old-friend/\">The Future of /Film: A Long-Awaited Redesign, a Newly https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-french-dispatch-e1626185910173-360x154.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/the-french-dispatch-e1626185910173-768x328.jpg 768w, Patron of Quirk, <strong>Wes Anderson</strong>, is back with a new film this year called <em><strong>The French Dispatch</strong></em>, a return to live action after taking a brief detour with 2018&#8217;s animated <em><strong>Isle of Dogs</strong></em>. Reviews out of the Cannes Film Festival have ratcheted up anticipation even higher, praising the distinctive auteur&#8217;s typically earnest approach, ambitious style, and masterful grasp of tone.</p>\n<p>Now, we can whet appetites even further with the newest clip released for the upcoming film, centering on a steamy (pun absolutely intended) interaction between a very unclothed <strong>Timothée Chalamet</strong> in the bath and <strong>Frances McDormand</strong>. Take a look for yourself.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-683249\"></span></p>\n<h2>The French Dispatch Clip</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/dvubfl-qeC8?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>To set the scene, <em>The French Dispatch</em> is very much an anthology film with each chapter dealing with its own specific storyline. As you may have gathered from this clip, this sequence revolves around a group of protestors — McDormand&#8217;s Lucinda Krementz has apparently just been tear-gassed (and is also sad, but most definitely not lonely) — during student riots in 1960s France. Zeffirelli (Chalamet) is boasting about his revolutionary manifesto, but Mrs. Krementz is&#8230;unimpressed, to say the least, and subsequently gets to work correcting typos and offering pointed critiques. Editors: can&#8217;t live with them and can&#8217;t live without &#8217;em, am I right?</p>\n<p>As one of those dorks who tries to avoid trailers for movies I know I&#8217;m going to watch, I have to admit I caved with this clip and am mildly blown away by just how well both McDormand and Chalamet acquit themselves with Anderson&#8217;s bone-dry dialogue and utterly deadpan sense of humor. Of course, this isn&#8217;t McDormand&#8217;s first go-around in a Wes Anderson film, as the popular actor also starred in the delightful <em><strong>Moonrise Kingdom</strong></em>, but Chalamet carries himself as if he were a longtime Anderson muse and seamlessly slides into this sneakily demanding role.</p>\n<p>Anderson has <a href=\"https://www.indiewire.com/2019/04/wes-anderson-french-dispatch-details-interview-release-date-1202059011/\">previously described his approach to this film</a>, saying:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;The story is not easy to explain. [It’s about an] American journalist based in France [who] creates his magazine. It is more a portrait of this man, of this journalist who fights to write what he wants to write. It’s not a movie about freedom of the press, but when you talk about reporters you also talk about what’s going on in the real world.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>As /Film&#8217;s Jason Gorber puts it in his<a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-french-dispatch-review-cannes/\"> review out of Cannes</a>, &#8220;It’s a film that weaponizes whimsy in ways that will dazzle die-hard fans of the director. As long as your heart is open, your ears attuned to the pace of the proceedings and eyes accustomed to this mode of staging, you’ll have a quite remarkable experience gorging on this gorgeous film.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Featuring an endlessly talented cast including (but not limited to) <strong>Bill Murray</strong>, <strong>Owen Wilson</strong>, <strong>Tilda Swinton</strong>, McDormand, <strong>Adrien Brody</strong>, <strong>Benicio Del Toro</strong>, <strong>Jeffrey Wright</strong>, <strong>Léa Seydoux</strong>, Chalamet, <strong>Elisabeth Moss</strong>, <strong>Edward Norton</strong>, <strong>Willem Dafoe</strong>, <strong>Saoirse Ronan</strong>, <strong>Christophe Waltz</strong>, and <strong>Jason Schwartzman</strong>, <em>The French Dispatch</em> arrives at a theater near you on <strong>July 24,</strong> <strong>2020</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\"
